## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of a (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear oscillator. Typical models include linear harmonic motion with damping, nonlinear restoring forces (Duffing), nonlinear damping (van der Pol/Rayleigh), and time-periodic forcing/parametric excitation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement; sign absorbed in c0)
- Viscous damping + linear spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-spring-damper in first-order form)
- Constant/bias acceleration: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * x + c2 * v (offset forces or linearization around shifted equilibrium)
- Coulomb (dry) friction term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (stick-slip approximated with velocity sign)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger nonlinear elasticity)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping in oscillatory motion)
- Rayleigh oscillator damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (self-excited oscillations via negative linear + positive cubic damping)
- van der Pol form (in x,v): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (state-dependent damping producing limit cycles)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle (sin restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (nonlinear restoring from geometry; damping optional)
- Softening via sine expansion: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (Taylor surrogate for sin-like restoring near equilibrium)
- External harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven oscillator response/resonance)
- Multi-tone forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (richer periodic drives)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametrically driven oscillator)
- Coupled nonlinearity (amplitude-dependent damping/stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (interaction between displacement and dissipation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: odd functions of x (x, x**3, sin(c*x)) indicate symmetric potentials and oscillations about x=0; adding a constant term shifts equilibrium.
- Energy-conserving structure: dv_dt depending only on x (no v, no t) suggests conservative motion with dv_dt = -dU/dx for some potential U(x).
- Linear damping signature: a term proportional to v produces exponential decay of amplitude in the linear regime and broadens resonance under forcing.
- Nonlinear drag/damping: terms like v*Abs(v) or v**3 produce amplitude-dependent decay rates (stronger damping at higher speeds).
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: negative effective damping at small amplitude with positive damping at large amplitude is often captured by (c0 + c1*x**2)*v or v - v**3-type structures.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: positive vs negative cubic stiffness (x**3 term) shifts the oscillation frequency upward vs downward with amplitude.
- Periodic forcing identification: sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms indicate externally driven oscillations; combinations imply multi-frequency excitation and possible beats.
- Parametric resonance: time-multiplying-x terms like cos(c*t)*x indicate modulation of stiffness and can generate resonance at half the natural frequency.
- Velocity sign term: sign(v) reflects dry friction, producing non-smooth dynamics, amplitude decay roughly linear in time, and possible stick-slip near vŌēł0.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO41)
============================================================
GT: -mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the ground truth:

$$GT = -0.493165631499977 \cdot v \cdot (1 - x^2) - 1.16769962902767 \cdot x \cdot e^{-|x|}$$

Expanding:
$$GT = -0.493165631499977 \cdot v + 0.493165631499977 \cdot v \cdot x^2 - 1.16769962902767 \cdot x \cdot e^{-|x|}$$

The key components are:
1. A term proportional to $v$
2. A term proportional to $v \cdot x^2$
3. A term $x \cdot e^{-|x|}$ ŌĆö this is the critical non-polynomial part

The function $x \cdot e^{-|x|}$ is the key basis function. No finite combination of polynomials, rational functions, logarithms, or algebraic functions can exactly equal $x \cdot e^{-|x|}$ for all $x$. Let me check each candidate for this basis function.

**Candidates with $x \cdot \exp(\cdot)$ terms:**
- **Candidate 4**: has $c8 \cdot x \cdot \exp(c9 \cdot x^2)$. We need $e^{-|x|}$, but $e^{c9 \cdot x^2}$ cannot equal $e^{-|x|}$ since $x^2 \neq -|x|$ generally. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with $\exp(c \cdot |v|)$ or $\exp(c \cdot v)$ terms:**
- Candidates 10, 26, 27, 29, 32, 43, 48, 50: These have exponentials in $v$, not producing $e^{-|x|}$. Setting the exponential coefficient to 0 reduces them to polynomial/rational forms. **NO MATCH**

**All other candidates** use combinations of: polynomials ($x, x^3, x^5, x^7, x^9$), rational functions ($x/(c+|x|)^n$), logarithmic terms ($x \cdot \log(c|x|+1)$, $x^3 \cdot \log(c|x|+1)$), cube roots, $\sin$, $\text{Max}$ functions, and linear terms in $v$ and $v \cdot x^2$.

The $v$ and $v \cdot x^2$ parts can be matched by appropriate constants. The critical question is whether any combination of the remaining basis functions can exactly equal $x \cdot e^{-|x|}$.

$x \cdot e^{-|x|}$ is an analytic function (on each half-line) with essential singularity behavior ŌĆö it decays exponentially. No finite sum of:
- Polynomials (grow without bound)
- Rational functions like $x/(c+|x|)^n$ (decay as power laws)
- $x \cdot \log(c|x|+1)$ (grows logarithmically)
- $x^3 \cdot \log(c|x|+1)$ (grows polynomially ├Ś log)
- Cube root terms (grow algebraically)
- Trigonometric terms

can exactly reproduce exponential decay. These are fundamentally different basis functions. The Taylor series of $e^{-|x|}$ is infinite, so no finite polynomial can match it. Rational functions decay as power laws, not exponentially. Logarithmic terms grow, not decay.

Therefore, **none** of the candidates can exactly match the ground truth, as none contain the basis function $e^{-|x|}$ (or any equivalent exponential in $|x|$).

Let me verify: Candidate 4 has $x \cdot \exp(c9 \cdot x^2)$ ŌĆö but $\exp(c \cdot x^2) \neq \exp(-|x|)$ for any constant $c$.
